## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration equation for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. With velocity v and time t as inputs, the acceleration dv/dt likely involves nonlinear damping/restoring terms in v and possibly periodic driving in t.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (simple viscous damping)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing-type): dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear restoring force in velocity)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v (amplitude-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh dissipation: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3 (nonlinear friction)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven + damped: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Duffing with driving)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v * abs(v) (aerodynamic drag)
- Polynomial in v: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 (general nonlinear velocity dependence)
- Cosine driving with damping: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (driven Duffing)
- Van der Pol driven: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (forced self-oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear oscillator)
- Mixed time-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * v * sin(c1 * t) (parametric excitation)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (Mathieu-type equation in v)
- General nonlinear + drive: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**2 + c2 * v**3 + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (comprehensive model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Self-sustained oscillation → terms like (1 - v²)*v indicating amplitude-dependent sign change in damping (Van der Pol structure)
- Odd-symmetry in velocity → only odd powers of v (v, v³, v⁵) indicating symmetric phase-space dynamics
- Periodic driving force → sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) as additive terms
- Parametric excitation → velocity multiplied by periodic function of time, v*sin(c*t), indicating time-varying system parameters
- Hardening/softening spring analogy → sign of cubic coefficient determines whether nonlinearity stiffens or softens response
- Negative linear damping with positive cubic damping → hallmark of limit cycle oscillators (energy balance at finite amplitude)
- Phase-shifted driving → sin(c*t + phi) needed when driving frequency and natural frequency create phase relationships
- Even powers of v breaking symmetry → v² terms indicate asymmetric dynamics or rectification effects
